# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the etcd client-side retry and timeout policy implementation. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I've created a detailed JSON document at `/workspace/answer.json` that identifies **9 key Go source files** and **20 critical symbols** implementing the client-side retry and timeout policy in etcd-io/etcd:

### Key Components Found:

1. **Retry Interceptor** (`client/v3/retry_interceptor.go`):
   - `unaryClientInterceptor` - Retry logic for unary gRPC calls
   - `streamClientInterceptor` - Retry logic for streaming (Watch, Lease)
   - `serverStreamingRetryingStream` - Stream buffering and retry for resilience
   - `waitRetryBackoff` - Exponential backoff with jitter

2. **Retry Policy** (`client/v3/retry.go`):
   - `isSafeRetryImmutableRPC` - Allows retry of reads (Get operations) on transient errors
   - `isSafeRetryMutableRPC` - Restricts retry of writes (Put, Delete) to protect write-at-most-once semantics
   - `RetryKVClient` - Wraps KV client with appropriate retry policies
   - `RetryLeaseClient` - Wraps Lease client with retry policies

3. **Endpoint Balancer** (`client/v3/internal/resolver/resolver.go`):
   - `EtcdManualResolver` - Manages endpoint resolution and round-robin load balancing

4. **Timeout Configuration** (`client/v3/config.go`):
   - `DialTimeout` - Connection establishment timeout
   - `DialKeepAliveTime` - Keepalive ping interval
   - `DialKeepAliveTimeout` - Keepalive response timeout

5. **Operation Implementations**:
   - `kv.go` - KV operations (Put, Get, Delete) with timeout enforcement
   - `watch.go` - Watch streams with retry on transient errors
   - `lease.go` - Lease operations with keepalive timeout management
   - `client.go` - Connection health check and dial setup with keepalive parame
... (truncated)

should\n381: // hold off for. \"text\": \"The etcd client-side retry and timeout policy is implemented across several key components in the GitHub repository github.com/etcd-io/etcd:\\n\\n## Retry Interceptor Implementation\\n\\nThe core retry logic is implemented in `client/v3/retry_interceptor.go`. This file contains two main interceptors:\\n\\n1. **unaryClientInterceptor** (line 41): Handles retry for unary gRPC calls. It implements a loop-based retry mechanism with configurable maximum retries, backoff strategies, and context deadline handling. For each failed attempt, it checks if the error is safe to retry using `isSafeRetry()`, manages token refresh for authentication failures, and respects context cancellations.\\n\\n2. **streamClientInterceptor** (line 112): Handles retry for server-side streaming calls. It wraps the stream in a `serverStreamingRetryingStream` (line 188) that buffers sent messages and implements `RecvMsg()` retry logic. This is critical for Watch operations which use bidirectional streaming.\\n\\nKey retry support functions include:\\n- **waitRetryBackoff** (line 312): Implements backoff delay between retries using `backoffLinearWithJitter` with a default 50ms jitter\\n- **isSafeRetry** (line 330 in retry_interceptor.go): Determines if an error is retryable based on error type and retry policy\\n\\n## Retry Policy and Safety Checks\\n\\nThe `client/v3/retry.go` file implements detailed retry safety logic:\\n\\n1. **isSafeRetryImmutableRPC** (line 54): Immutable requests (Get) can be safely retried on any transient error except server-specific errors like ErrCompacted. Only retries on `codes.Unavailable`.\\n\\n2. **isSafeRetryMutableRPC** (line 85): Mutable requests (Put, Delete, Txn) can only be retried when there's no connection available (`codes.Unavailable` with specific error descriptions). This enforces write-at-most-once semantics.\\n\\n3. **RetryKVClient** (line 101): Wraps the KV client to apply retry policies. Range operations use `withRepeatablePolicy()` for retries, while Put/Delete/Txn operations follow the default non-repeatable policy.\\n\\n4. **RetryLeaseClient** (line 132): Similar wrapper for Lease operations, marking read operations as repeatable.\\n\\n## Endpoint Balancer and Resolver\\n\\nThe `client/v3/internal/resolver/resolver.go` file implements:\\n\\n1. **EtcdManualResolver** (line 31): A gRPC resolver that maintains the list of available endpoints and updates the load balancer. It uses `round_robin` load balancing policy (line 44) and supports dynamic endpoint updates via `SetEndpoints()`.\\n\\n2. **updateState** (line 62): Converts endpoint strings to gRPC resolver endpoints with proper address and server name interpretation for TLS validation.\\n\\nThe resolver is integrated into the client dial process through `dialWithBalancer()` in client.go (line 310-322), which uses the resolver to provide endpoints to the gRPC connection.\\n\\n## Timeout and KeepAlive Configuration\\n\\nThe `client/v3/config.go` file defines critical timeout parameters:\\n\\n1. **DialTimeout** (line 36-37): Timeout for establishing initial connection, used in `dialSetupOpts()` with `context.WithTimeout()`\\n\\n2. **DialKeepAliveTime** (line 39-41): Time interval between client-to-server keepalive pings\\n\\n3. **DialKeepAliveTimeout** (line 43-45): Timeout waiting for keepalive response before closing connection\\n\\n4. **PermitWithoutStream** (line 64): Allows keepalive pings even without active RPCs\\n\\nThese are applied in `client/v3/client.go` at line 227-237 in the `dialSetupOpts()` function using `keepalive.ClientParameters`.\\n\\n## Connection Health Check\\n\\nThe `waitForConnection()` function (line 344 in client.go) performs a gRPC health check before accepting the connection:\\n- Uses `healthpb.NewHealthClient().Check()` with `grpc.WaitForReady(true)`\\n- Tolerates `Unimplemented` (server without health endpoint) and `FailedPrecondition` (leader not yet applied config)\\n- Implements timeout using `withMax(0)` to disable retry on health check failures\\n\\n## KV Operations\\n\\nThe `client/v3/kv.go` file implements:\\n\\n1. **kv struct** (line 96): Contains the remote KV client and call options\\n\\n2. **Put/Get/Delete** (lines 117-130): High-level operations that wrap the lower-level `Do()` method. They use `ContextError()` to wrap context errors appropriately.\\n\\n3. **NewKV** (line 101): Creates a KV client with `RetryKVClient()` wrapper to enable retry logic\\n\\nRequest timeout for KV operations is enforced through context passed by the caller using `context.WithTimeout()`.\\n\\n## Watch Operations\\n\\nThe `client/v3/watch.go` file implements streaming watch functionality:\\n\\n1. **watcher struct** (line 144): Manages watch streams and maintains a map of active watchers\\n\\n2. **watchGRPCStream** (line 156): Handles individual gRPC streams, buffering watch responses\\n\\n3. **Watch** (line 82): Creates a watch channel for monitoring key changes. The stream interceptor retries on transient errors while preserving watch semantics.\\n\\nWatch timeout is managed through context passed to the Watch call, with streaming retry handled by `streamClientInterceptor()`.\\n\\n## Lease Operations\\n\\nThe `client/v3/lease.go` file implements lease management:\\n\\n1. **lessor struct** (line 151): Manages lease state and keepalive multiplexing\\n\\n2. **keepAlive struct** (line 181): Tracks keepalive deadline and timeout, with `firstKeepAliveTimeout` default of `DialTimeout + 1 second` (line 193)\\n\\n3. **KeepAlive** (line 122-138): Continuously renews leases.
